<div xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml"><p>This page describes information about fields that are used for advanced searching. A field in JQL is a word that represents a Jira field (or a custom field that has already been defined in your Jira applications). In a clause, a field is followed by an <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/advanced-searching-operators-reference-1488596776.html">operator</a>, which in turn is followed by one or more values (orÂ  <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/advanced-searching-functions-reference-1488596777.html">functions</a>). The operator compares the value of the field with one or more values or functions on the right, such that only true results are retrieved by the clause. Note: it is not possible to compare two fields in JQL.</p><h2>Affected version</h2> <p>Search for issues that are assigned to a particular affects version(s). You can search by version name or version ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a version).Note, it is better to search by version ID than by version name. Different projects may have versions with the same name. It is also possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a version, which could break any saved filters that rely on that name. Version IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>affectedVersion</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>VERSION</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1">Yes</td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>
                    <strong>= , != , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= , ~ </strong>, <strong> <code>!~ </code> </strong> </code> <br /> <code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN </code></strong></p> <ul><li><em>The comparison operators (e.g. "&gt;") use the version order that has been set up by your project administrator, not a numeric or alphabetic order.</em></li><li><em>For this field, the contain operators (~ and!~) find exact matches, and can be used to search through versions with a wildcard.</em></li></ul></td></tr><tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><br /> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">When used with the <strong>IN</strong> Â andÂ  <strong>NOT IN</strong> Â operators, this field supports:<ul><li><span>releasedVersions</span> ()</li> <li><span>latestReleasedVersion</span> ()</li> <li><span>unreleasedVersions</span> ()</li> <li><span>earliestUnreleasedVersion</span> ()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find issues with an AffectedVersion of 3.14:<br /> <code>affectedVersion = "3.14"</code> <br /> <em><sub>Note that full-stops are reserved <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">characters</a> and need to be surrounded by quote-marks.</sub></em></li><li>Find issues with an AffectedVersion of "Big Ted":<br /> <code>affectedVersion = "Big Ted"</code></li> <li>Find issues with an AffectedVersion ID of 10350:<br /> <code>affectedVersion = 10350</code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Approvals</h2> <p><em>Only applicable if Jira Service Management is installed and licensed, and you're using the Approvals functionality.</em></p><p>Search for issues that have been approved or require approval.                       <span>approval = pendingBy(jsmith)</span>
                    </code></p></li> <li><p>Find issues that require approval by the current user:<br /> <code>approval = myPending()</code></p></li> <li><p>Find all issues that require approval:<br /> <code>approval = pending()</code></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Assignee</h2> <p>Search for issues that are assigned to a particular user. You can search by the user's full name, ID, or email address.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>assignee</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Alias</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>cf[CustomFieldID]</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>USER</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>
                    <strong>= , != </strong>                  </code> <br /> <code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN, <strong> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code> </strong> </code></strong></p> <p><em>Note that the comparison operators (e.g. "&gt;") use the version order that has been set up by your project administrator, not a numeric or alphabetic order.</em></p></td></tr><tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>~ , !~ <strong> <code>
                      <strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </strong>
                    </code> </strong> </code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">When used with the <strong>IN</strong> Â andÂ  <strong>NOT IN</strong> Â operators, this field supports:<ul><li>membersOf()</li></ul> <p>When used with the <strong>EQUALS</strong> Â andÂ  <strong>NOT EQUALS</strong> operators, this field supports:</p><ul><li>currentUser()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li><p>Find issues that are assigned to John Smith:<br /> <code>assignee = "John Smith"<br />
                    </code> or <code>
                      <br />assignee = jsmith</code></p></li> <li><p>Find issues that are currently assigned, or were previously assigned, to John Smith:<br /> <code>assignee WAS "John Smith"Â <br />
                    </code> or <code>
                      <br />assignee WAS jsmith</code></p></li> <li><p>Find issues that are assigned by the user with email address "bob@mycompany.com":<br /> <code>assignee = "bob@mycompany.com"</code></p> <p><em><sub>Note that full-stops and "@" symbols are reserved <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">characters</a> and need to be surrounded by quote-marks.</sub></em></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div><p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Attachments</h2> <p>Search for issues that have or do not have attachments. </p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>attachments</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>ATTACHMENT</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1">Yes</td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><strong><strong><code>IS, IS NOT</code></strong></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><code>=, != , ~ , !~ <strong> <code>
                        <strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</strong>                      </code> </strong> </code></strong> <strong><code>IN, NOT IN, <strong> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code> </strong> </code></strong></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">None</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li><p>Search for issues that have attachments:<br /> <code>attachments IS NOT EMPTY</code></p></li> <li><p>Search for issues that do not have attachments:<br /> <code>attachments IS EMPTY</code></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Category</h2> <p>Search for issues that belong to projects in a particular category.</p><div><table><tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>category</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>CATEGORY</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1">Yes</td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><strong><strong><code>=, !=</code></strong> <br /> <strong><code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN</code></strong></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><code>~ , !~ <strong> <code>
                        <strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</strong>
</code> </strong> </code></strong> <strong><code>
                    <strong> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code> </strong> </code></strong></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">None</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li><p>Find issues that belong to projects in the "Alphabet Projects" Category:<br /> <code>category = "Alphabet Projects"</code></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <p>Search for issues that have a comment that contains particular text. <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">Jira text-search syntax</a> can be used.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>comment</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>TEXT</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>~ , !~</code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>= , != , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </strong> </code> <br /><code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN, </code> </strong> </code><code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">None</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find issues where a comment contains text that matches "My PC is quite old" (i.e. a "fuzzy" match:<br /> <code>comment ~ "My PC is quite old"</code></li> <li>Find issues where a comment contains the exact phrase "My PC is quite old":<br /> <code>comment ~ "\"My PC is quite old\""</code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Component</h2> <p>Search for issues that belong to a particular component(s) of a project. You can search by component name or component ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a component).</p><p>Note, it is safer to <em>search by component ID than by component name</em>. Different projects may have components with the same name, so searching by component name may return issues from multiple projects. It is also possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a component, which could break any saved filters that rely on that name. Component IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>component</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>COMPONENT</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , != <br />IS , IS NOT , IN , NOT IN </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </strong> </code> <br /></strong> </code> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>When used with the <strong>IN</strong> and <strong>NOT IN</strong> operators, component supports:</p><ul><li>componentsLeadByUser()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find issues in the "Comp1" or "Comp2" component:<br /> <code>component in (Comp1, Comp2)</code></li> <li>Find issues in the "Comp1" and"Comp2" components:<br /> <code>
                    <span>component in (Comp1) and component in (Comp2)</span>
                    <br />or<br />
                    <span>component = Comp1 and component = Comp2</span>Â </code></li> <li>Find issues in the component with ID 20500:<code>
                    <br />
                    <code>component =Â </code> <code>20500</code>Â </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Created</h2> <p>Search for issues that were created on, before, or after a particular date (or date range). Note that if a time-component is not specified, midnight will be assumed. Please note that the search results will be relative to your configured time zone (which is by default the Jira instance's time zone).</p><p>Use one of the following formats:</p><p><code>"yyyy/MM/dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy/MM/dd"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd"</code></p> <p>Or use <code>"w"</code> (weeks), <code>"d"</code> (days), <code>"h"</code> (hours) or <code>"m"</code> (minutes) to specify a date relative to the current time. The default is <code>"m"</code> (minutes). Be sure to use quote-marks (<code>"</code>); if you omit the quote-marks, the number you supply will be interpreted as milliseconds after epoch (1970-1-1).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>created</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Alias</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>createdDate</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>DATE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , != , <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong>&gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= <br /> </strong>
                          </code> </strong> </code> </strong>IS , IS NOT , IN , NOT IN </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ </strong>
                    </code> <br /></strong> </code> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>When used with the <strong>EQUALS</strong>, <strong>NOT EQUALS</strong>, <strong>GREATER THAN</strong>, <strong>GREATER THAN EQUALS</strong>, <strong>LESS THAN</strong> or <strong>LESS THAN EQUALS</strong> operators, this field supports:</p><ul><li>currentLogin()</li> <li>lastLogin()</li> <li>now()</li> <li>startOfDay()</li> <li>startOfWeek()</li> <li>startOfMonth()</li> <li>startOfYear()</li> <li>endOfDay()</li> <li>endOfWeek()</li> <li>endOfMonth()</li> <li>endOfYear()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find all issues created before 12th December 2010:<br /> <code>created &lt;Â </code> <code>"2010/12/12"</code></li> <li>Find all issues created on or before 12th December 2010:<br /> <code>
                    <code>created &lt;=Â </code> <code>"2010/12/13"</code> </code></li> <li>Find all issues created on 12th December 2010 before 2:00pm:<code>
                    <br />
                    <code>created &gt;Â </code> <code>"2010/12/12"</code>Â <code>and created &lt;Â </code> <code>"2010/12/12 14:00"</code>Â </code></li> <li>Find issues created less than one day ago:<br /> <code>created &gt;Â </code> <code>"-1d"</code></li> <li>Find issues created in January 2011:<br /> <code>created &gt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/01"</code> <code>and created &lt;Â </code> <code>"2011/02/01"</code></li> <li><code>Find issues created on 15 January 2011:<br />
                  </code><code>
                    <code>created &gt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/15"</code>Â <code>and created &lt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/16"</code> </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Creator</h2> <p>Search for issues that were created by a particular user. You can search by the user's full name, ID, or email address.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>creator</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>USER</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , != <br />IS , IS NOT , IN , NOT IN, <strong> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN</code> </strong> </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </strong> </code> <br /></strong> </code> <code>CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>When used with the <strong>IN </strong> and <strong>NOT IN </strong> operators, this field supports:</p><ul><li><span>membersOf</span> ()</li></ul> <p>When used with the <strong>EQUALS </strong> and <strong>NOT EQUALS</strong> operators, this field supports:</p><ul><li><span>currentUser</span> ()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Search for issues that were created by Jill Jones:<br /> <code>creator =Â </code> <code>"Jill Jones"<br />or<br />creator = "jjones"</code></li> <li>Search for issues that were created by the user with email address "bob@mycompany.com":<br /> <code>
                    <code>creator =Â </code> <code>"bob@mycompany.com"<br />
                      <em> <sub>(Note that full-stops and "@" symbols are reservedÂ <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">characters</a>, so the email address needs to be surrounded by quote-marks.)</sub>Â </em>
                    </code> </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Custom field</h2> <p><em>Only applicable if your Jira administrator has created one or more custom fields.</em></p><p>Search for issues where a particular custom field has a particular value. You can search by custom field name or custom field ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to an custom field).</p><p>Note, it is safer to search by custom field ID than by custom field name. It is possible for a custom field to have the same name as a built-in Jira system field; in which case, Jira will search for the system field (not your custom field). It is also possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a custom field, which could break any saved filters that rely on that name. Custom field IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>CustomFieldName</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Alias</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>cf[CustomFieldID]</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td><em>Depends on the custom field's configuration <br /></em> <p><em>Note, <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">Jira text-search syntax</a> can be used with custom fields of type 'Text'.</em></p></td></tr><tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes, for custom fields of type picker, group picker, select, checkbox and radio button fields</p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><p><em>Different types of custom field support different operators.</em></p></td></tr><tr><th>Supported operators: <br /> number and date fields </th> <td><p><strong><code>= , != , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; . &lt;= <br />IS , IS NOT , IN , NOT IN </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators: <br /> number and date fields</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ </strong>
                    </code> <br /></strong> </code> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported operators: <br /> picker, select, checkbox <br /> and radio button fields</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>= , != <br />IS , IS NOT , IN , NOT IN </code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators: <br /> picker, select, checkbox <br /> and radio button fields</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ , <strong> <code>&gt; , &gt;= , &lt; . &lt;= </code> </strong> </strong> </code> <br /></strong> </code> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported operators: <br /> text fields </th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>

                  </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Customer Request Type</h2> <p><em>Only applicable if Jira Service Management is installed and licensed.</em></p><p>Search for Issues matching a specific Customer Request Type in a service desk project. The search is based on either the epic's name, issue key, or issue ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to an issue).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>"epic link"</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>Epic Link Relationship</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , !=</code></strong> <strong><code>
                    <br />IS , IS NOT, <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>

                  <strong> <code>

                    <code>"epic link"</code>Â <code>= Jupiter</code> </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Filter</h2> <p>You can use a saved filter to narrow your search. You can search by filter name or filter ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a saved filter).</p><p>Note:</p><ul><li>It is safer to search by filter ID than by filter name. It is possible for a filter name to be changed, which could break a saved filter that invokes another filter by name. Filter IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</li><li>An unnamed link statement in your typed query will override an ORDER BY statement in the saved filter.</li><li>You cannot run or save a filter that would cause an infinite loop (i.e. you cannot reference a saved filter if it eventually references your current filter).</li></ul><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>filter</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Aliases</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>request , savedFilter , searchRequest</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>Filter</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , !=</code></strong> <strong><code>
                    <br />
                    <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong> <code>
                                <strong> <code>
                                    <strong> <code>
                                        <strong> <code>IN , NOT IN</code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><code>
                    <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong> <strong> <code>
                                  <strong> <code>
                                      <strong> <strong> <code>
                                            <strong> <code>
                                                <strong> <strong> <code>
                                                      <strong> <code>
                                                          <strong> <code>
                                                              <strong>~ , !~ </strong>
                                                            </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code></strong> <code>
                  <strong>  <br /></strong> </code> <code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong> <code>
                          <strong> <code>IS , IS NOT, </code> </strong>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN</code> </strong> , </code> </strong>CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>None</p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Search the results of the filter "My Saved Filter" (which has an ID of 12000) for issues assigned to the user jsmith:<br /> <code>
                    <code>filter =Â </code> <code>"My Saved Filter"</code>Â <code>and assignee = jsmith</code> <br />or<br /><code>filter =Â </code> <code>12000</code>Â <code>and assignee = jsmith</code> <br /></code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Fix version</h2> <p>Search for issues that are assigned to a particular fix version. You can search by version name or version ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a version).</p><p>Note, it is safer to search by version ID than by version name. Different projects may have versions with the same name, so searching by version name may return issues from multiple projects. It is also possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a version, which could break any saved filters that rely on that name. Version IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>fixVersion</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>VERSION</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>
                      <strong> <code>= , != </code> </strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= , ~ , <strong> <strong> <code>

For example, an issue may</span> <em><span>duplicate</span></em> <span>another issue or</span> <em><span>depend</span></em> <span>on the resolution of another issue</span>.<span>You can find detailed information about issue links in</span> <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/adminjiraserver0820/configuring-issue-linking-1095777745.html"><span>Configuring issue linking</span></a><span>. </span></p><p>When searching for issues with a particular link type, you can only find linked issues that are on the same Jira instance you're searching on. Links to issues on a remote Jira instance or to Confluence pages won't be included.</p><p>Use the following JQL query to add colors to your issue cards! For example, add a red stripe to issues that have some blockers, and keep all other issues green. This will help you bring the right information to your teamâ€™s attention, at a glance.                     </code></li> <li>Find issues with an issue type of "duplicates" or "is duplicated by":<br /> <code>issueLinkType in (duplicates,"is duplicated by")</code></li> <li>Find issues with link types other than â€œclonesâ€:<br /> <code>issueLinkType != clones</code> <br /> <span>This query will also return issues with no links at all.</span></li><li><span>Find issues that are blocker by other issues, or that don't have any blockers.</span><br /> <span><code>
                        <span>issueLinkType = "is blocked by"</span>
                      </code> <br /></span> <span><span><code>

                        </code></span></span></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <p>Search for issues tagged with a label or list of labels. You can also search for issues without any labels to easily identify which issues need to be tagged so they show up in the relevant sprints, queues or reports. </p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>labels</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>LABEL</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>
                    <strong>= , <strong> <code>
                          <strong> <code>
                              <strong>!=, </strong>
                            </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </strong> </code><code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN </code></strong></p> <p><em>We recommend using IS or IS NOT to search for a single label, and IN or NOT IN to search for a list of labels.</em></p></td></tr><tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>~ , !~ , <strong> <code>
                      <strong>, <strong> <code>
                            <strong>&gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </strong>
                          </code> </strong> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> <br /> <code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1">None</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find issues with an existing label:<br /> <code>labels = "x"</code></li> <li>Find issues without a specified label, including issues without a label:<br /> <code>labels not in ("x") or labels is EMPTY</code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <h2>Last viewed</h2> <p>Search for issues that were last viewed on, before, or after a particular date (or date range). Note that if a time-component is not specified, midnight will be assumed. Please note that the search results will be relative to your configured time zone (which is by default the Jira instance's time zone).</p><p>Use one of the following formats:</p><p><code>"yyyy/MM/dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy/MM/dd"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd"</code></p> <p>Or use <code>"w"</code> (weeks), <code>"d"</code> (days), <code>"h"</code> (hours) or <code>"m"</code> (minutes) to specify a date relative to the current time. The default is <code>"m"</code> (minutes). Be sure to use quote-marks (<code>"</code>); if you omit the quote-marks, the number you supply will be interpreted as milliseconds after epoch (1970-1-1).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>lastViewed</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>DATE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>
                      <strong> <code>= , != </code> </strong>, &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</code></strong></strong> <strong><code>
                    <br />IS , IS NOT, <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong> <code>
                                <strong> <code>
                                    <strong> <code>
                                        <strong> <code>IN , NOT IN</code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code> </strong> </code></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><code>
                    <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong> <strong> <code>

You can search by issue level security name or issue level security ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to an issue level security).</p><p>Note, it is safer to search by security level ID than by security level name. It is possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a security level, which could break any saved filter that rely on that name. Security level IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>level</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>SECURITY LEVEL</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>= , != </code></strong></strong> <strong><code>

Please note that the search results will be relative to your configured time zone (which is by default the Jira instance's time zone).</p><p>Use one of the following formats:</p><p><code>"yyyy/MM/dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy/MM/dd"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd"</code></p> <p>Or use <code>"w"</code> (weeks), <code>"d"</code> (days), <code>"h"</code> (hours) or <code>"m"</code> (minutes) to specify a date relative to the current time. The default is <code>"m"</code> (minutes). Be sure to use quote-marks (<code>"</code>); if you omit the quote-marks, the number you supply will be interpreted as milliseconds after epoch (1970-1-1).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>request-last-activity-time</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>DATE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><p><strong><code>= , != , &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</code></strong></p> <p><strong><code>IS, IS NOT, IN, NOT IN</code></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators </th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><code>

You can search by resolution name or resolution ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a resolution).</p><p>Note, it is safer to search by resolution ID than by resolution name. <span>It is possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a resolution, which could break any saved filter that rely on that name. Resolution IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</span></p><div><table><tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>resolution</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td><span>RESOLUTION</span></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>= , != , </code></strong></strong><strong><strong><strong><code>&gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= </code></strong></strong></strong> <strong><code>

elapsed("1h")</code></p></li> <li><p><code>Find issues that that will breach Time to First Response in the next two hours:<br />"Time to First Response" &lt; remaining("2h")</code></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Sprint</h2> <p>Search for issues that are assigned to a particular sprint. This works for active sprints and future sprints. The search is based on either the sprint name or the sprint ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a sprint).</p><p>If you have multiple sprints with similar (or identical) names, you can simply search by using the sprint name â€” or even just part of it. The possible matches will be shown in the autocomplete drop-down, with the sprint dates shown to help you distinguish between them. (The sprint ID will also be shown, in brackets).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>sprint</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td><span>NUMBER</span></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>= , != </code></strong></strong> <strong><code>

You can search by status name or status ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to a status).</p><p>Note:</p><ul><li>It is safer to search by status ID than status name. <span>It is possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a status, which could break any saved filter that rely on that name. Status IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</span></li><li>The WAS, WAS NOT, WAS IN and WAS NOT IN operators can only be used with the name, not the ID.</li></ul><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>status</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td><span>STATUS</span></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>= , != </code></strong></strong> <strong><code>

Each issue status in Jira can belong to one of the three status categories: <strong>To Do</strong>, <strong>In Progress</strong>, or <strong>Done</strong>. You can't add or remove status categories.</p><p>These status categories represent and generalize the three main stages of an ideal issue workflow. Each issue goes from the stage where the work on it hasn't started yet, through the stage when you're working on it, to the stage when the work on has been completed.</p><p>These stages can have multiple statuses that you set for your custom workflow. For example, the custom statuses "In development" and "In review" can belong to the single status category <strong>In Progress</strong>, because they represent the stage where you're developing and reviewing a feature described in the issue.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>statusCategory</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Aliases</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>New, Indeterminate, Complete</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td><span>STATUS</span></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , !=, </code></strong><strong><code>IN , NOT INÂ </code></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><p><strong><code>
                        
                             
                                 
                                      
                                           
                                                
                                                     
                                                          
                                                               
                                                                   
                                                                      ~ , !~ , 
                                                                                           &gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;=</code></strong></p> <p><strong><code>IS , IS NOT, WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN , CHANGED</code></strong> <strong><br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>None</p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li><span>Find issues with the status category "To Do":</span><br /> <span><code><span>statusCategory = "To Do"</span></code></span></li> <li><span>Find issues with the status category ID <code>3</code> where <code>3</code> stands for closed issues:</span><br /> <code>statusCategory =Â </code> <span>3</span></li> <li><span>Find all issues that are currently in progress:</span><br /> <code>statusCategory not in ("To Do", "Done")</code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Summary</h2> <p>Search for issues where the summary contains particular text. <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/search-syntax-for-text-fields-1488596778.html">Jira text-search syntax</a> can be used.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>summary</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>TEXT</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><code>~ , !~ </code></strong></strong> <strong><code>

                    <br />
                  </code></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><strong><strong><code>

You can search by issue type name or issue type ID (i.e. the number that Jira automatically allocates to an issue type).</p><p>Note, it is safer to search by type ID than type name. It is possible for your Jira administrator to change the name of a type, which could break any saved filter that rely on that name. Type IDs, however, are unique and cannot be changed.</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>type</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Alias</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>issueType</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>ISSUE_TYPE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><strong><code>= , !=</code></strong></strong></strong> <strong><strong><code> <br />

                    <code>issueType =Â </code> <code>2</code> </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Updated</h2> <p>Search for issues that were last updated on, before, or after a particular date (or date range). Note that if a time-component is not specified, midnight will be assumed. Please note that the search results will be relative to your configured time zone (which is by default the Jira instance's time zone).</p><p>Use one of the following formats:</p><p><code>"yyyy/MM/dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy/MM/dd"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd"</code></p> <p>Or use <code>"w"</code> (weeks), <code>"d"</code> (days), <code>"h"</code> (hours) or <code>"m"</code> (minutes) to specify a date relative to the current time. The default is <code>"m"</code> (minutes). Be sure to use quote-marks (<code>"</code>); if you omit the quote-marks, the number you supply will be interpreted as milliseconds after epoch (1970-1-1).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>updated</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Alias</th> <td colspan="1"><pre><code>updatedDate</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>DATE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><strong><code>= , !=</code></strong></strong></strong> <strong><strong><code> , <strong> <strong> <strong> <code>

"2010/12/13"</code></li> <li>Find all issues that were last updated before 2.00pm on 31st December 2010:<br /> <code>updated &lt; "2010/12/31 14:00"</code></li> <li>Find issues that were last updated more than two weeks ago:<br /> <code>updated &lt;Â </code> <code>"-2w"</code></li> <li>Find issues that were last updated on 15 January 2011:<br /> <code>updated &gt; "2011/01/15" and updated &lt; "2011/01/16"</code></li> <li>Find issues that were last updated in January 2011:<br /> <code>updated &gt; "2011/01/01" and updated &lt; "2011/02/01"</code></li> <li>Find all issues updated since January 1, 2020:<br /> <code>updated &gt;= "2020/01/01"</code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Voter</h2> <p>Search for issues for which a particular user has voted. You can search by the user's full name, ID, or email address. Note that you can only find issues for which you have the "View Voters and Watchers" permission, unless you are searching for your own votes. See also <a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-votedIssues">votedIssues</a>.</p><div><table><tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>voter</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>USER</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>Yes</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><strong><strong><code>= , !=</code></strong></strong></strong> <strong><strong><code> <br />

                  </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Watcher</h2> <p>Search for issues that a particular user is watching. You can search by the user's full name, ID, or email address. Note that you can only find issues for which you have the "View Voters and Watchers" permission, unless you are searching for issues where you are the watcher.                     <span>watcher = currentUser()</span>
                  </code></li> <li>Search for issues that the user "jsmith" is watching:<br /> <code>
                    <span>watcher = "jsmith"</span>
                  </code></li> <li>Search for issues that are being watched by a member of the group "Jira-administrators":<br /> <code>
                    <span>watcher in membersOf("Jira-administrators")</span>
                  </code> <code>

                    <span>watchers &gt; 3</span>
                  </code></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Work log author</h2> <p><em>Only available if time-tracking has been enabled by your Jira administrator.</em></p><p>Search for issues a particular user has logged work against. You can search by the user's full name, ID, or email address.                       <code>summary ~Â </code> <code>"\"test sessions\""</code> </code></span></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Work log date</h2> <p><em>Only available if time-tracking has been enabled by your Jira administrator.</em></p><p>Search for issues that have comments in work log entries that were created on, before, or after a particular date (or date range). Please note that the search results are <span>stored as a local date in the search index (are <em>not</em></span> <span> relative to your configured time zone).</span></p><p>Use one of the following formats:</p><p><code>"yyyy/MM/dd"</code> <br /> <code>"yyyy-MM-dd"</code></p> <p>Or use <code>"w"</code> (weeks) or <code>"d"</code> (days) to specify a date relative to the current time. Be sure to use quote-marks (<code>"</code>); if you omit the quote-marks, the number you supply will be interpreted as milliseconds after epoch (1970-1-1).</p><div><table><colgroup><col /> <col /></colgroup> <tbody><tr><th>Syntax</th> <td><pre><code>worklogDate</code></pre></td></tr> <tr><th>Field Type</th> <td>DATE</td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Auto-complete</th> <td colspan="1"><p>No</p></td></tr> <tr><th>Supported operators</th> <td><p><strong><code>= , != , <strong> <code>
                        <strong> <code>
                            <strong>&gt; , &gt;= , &lt; , &lt;= <br /></strong></code></strong></code></strong>IN , NOT IN </code> <br /></strong></p></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Unsupported operators</th> <td colspan="1"><strong><code>
                  <strong> <code>
                      <strong>~ , !~ </strong>
                    </code> <br /></strong></code> <code>IS, IS NOT,Â </code><code>WAS, WAS IN, WAS NOT, WAS NOT IN, CHANGED</code></strong></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Supported functions</th> <td colspan="1"><p>When used with the <strong>EQUALS</strong>, <strong>NOT EQUALS</strong>, <strong>GREATER THAN</strong>, <strong>GREATER THAN EQUALS</strong>, <strong>LESS THAN</strong> or <strong>LESS THAN EQUALS</strong> operators, this field supports:</p><ul><li>currentLogin()</li> <li>lastLogin()</li> <li>now()</li> <li>startOfDay()</li> <li>startOfWeek()</li> <li>startOfMonth()</li> <li>startOfYear()</li> <li>endOfDay()</li> <li>endOfWeek()</li> <li>endOfMonth()</li> <li>endOfYear()</li></ul></td></tr> <tr><th colspan="1">Examples</th> <td colspan="1"><ul><li>Find issues that have comments in work log entries created before midnight 00:00 12th December 2010:<br /> <code>worklogDate &lt;Â </code> <code>"2010/12/12"</code></li> <li>Find issues that have comments in work log entries created on or before 12th December 2010 (but not 13th December 2010):<br /> <code>
                    <code>worklogDate &lt;=Â </code> <code>"2010/12/13"</code></code></li> <li>Find issues that have comments in work log entries created less than one day ago:<br /> <code>worklogDate &gt;Â </code> <code>"-1d"</code></li> <li>Find issues that have comments in work log entries created in January 2011:<br /> <code>worklogDate &gt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/01"</code> <code>and worklogDate &lt;Â </code> <code>"2011/02/01"</code></li> <li><p>Find issues that have comments in work log entries created on 15 January 2011:<br /> <code>
                      <code>worklogDate &gt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/15"</code>Â <code>and worklogDate &lt;Â </code> <code>"2011/01/16"</code> </code></p></li></ul></td></tr></tbody></table></div> <p><strong><sup><a href="https://confluence.atlassian.com/servicemanagementserver103/#Advancedsearchingfieldsreference-fields">^ top of page</a></sup></strong></p> <h2>Work ratio</h2> <p><em>Only available if time-tracking has been enabled by your Jira administrator.</em></p><p>Search for issues where the work ratio has a particular value.
